The Rule of Ta'arud Between Positive and Negative Evidence
Stating the rule for when a negative equals a positive in conflict

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a negative statement only conflicts with a positive if it is based on clear evidence, and identify the two categories that make a negative equivalent to a positive.

Core Idea
A negative only conflicts with a positive when it is based on evidence, not on istishab.

This passage from Noorul Anwar addresses a critical issue in Hanafi usul: when does a negative report (nafi) actually conflict with a positive report (ithbat)? The answer determines which narration is given precedence when both appear contradictory. The text presents two positions within the Hanafi school—that of Ibn Aban and al-Karkhi—and uses the famous case of Barirah to illustrate the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Begin by understanding the core principle: a negative statement can be equivalent to a positive if it is based on evidence (dalil) and not on istishab (presumption of continuity).
The passage starts by establishing this principle.
2
Identify the two categories
Find the two categories where the negative is considered equivalent: (1) when it is based on a clear proof and sign, and (2) when its basis is ambiguous but the narrator is known to rely on evidence.
These categories make the negative 'like the positive'.
3
Distinguish the two Hanafi views
Note that Ibn Aban holds that in these two categories the negative creates a conflict requiring tarjih, while al-Karkhi holds that if the negative is not based on evidence, the positive prevails without conflict.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Apply to the Barirah case
Apply the rule to the hadith of Barirah: one report says her husband was a slave (negative, based on original state), another says he became free (positive, based on evidence). Determine which report takes precedence based on the categories.
The example demonstrates the practical application.
5
Extract the outcome
According to al-Karkhi's view (which is preferred by later Hanafis), the positive report is given precedence, so the freed woman has the option to annul the marriage regardless of her husband's status.
This shows the thamarah al-khilaf of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التعارض بيان وقوع التعارض بين القياسين والأصل فيه أن النفي إن كان من جنس ما يعرف بدليله بأن كان مبنيا على دليل وعلامة ظاهرة، ولا يكون مبنيًا على الاستصحاب الذي ليس بحجة أو كان مما يشتبه حاله لكن عرف أن الراوي اعتمد دليل المعرفة، يعني كان النفي في نفسه مما يحتمل أن يكون مستفادًا من الدليل، وأن يكون مبنيا على الاستصحاب، لكن لما تفحص حال الراوي علم أنه اعتمد على الدليل ولم يبنه على صرف ظاهر الحال، ففي هاتين الصورتين كان مثل الإثبات؛ لأن الإثبات لا يكون إلا بالدليل، فإذا كان النفي أيضا بالدليل كان مثله، فيتعارض بينهما، ويحتاج بعد ذلك إلى دفعه، فجاء حينئذٍ مذهب ابن أبان. وإلا فلا أي إن لم يكن النفي من جنس ما يعرف بدليله ولا مما عرف أن الراوي اعتمد على الدليل، بل بناه على ظاهر الحال الماضية فلا يكون مثل الإثبات في معارضته بل الإثبات أولى؛ لأنه ثابت بالدليل، فجاء حينئذٍ مذهب الكرخي، فنحن نحتاج حينئذ إلى ثلاثة أمثلة: مثالين فيه أي في تعارض المثبت والنافي. (القمر) على الاستصحاب أي الإبقاء على ما كان عليه. (القمر) يشتبه حاله إلخ معنى اشتباه الحال أنه يعرف تارة بالدليل وتارة بالأصل. (السنبلي) هاتين الصورتين إلخ أي في صورة كونه من جنس ما يعرف بدليله وفي صورة كونه مشتبه الحال. قوله: مثل الإثبات إلخ، يعني كان النفي مثل الإثبات، فيتعارضان كلاهما أي النفي والإثبات ويطلب الترجيح لأحدهما خارج ليندفع التعارض، وقوله : "وإلا" "فلا" معناه إن لم يكن النفي من أحد القسمين المذكورين، فلا يكون النفي مثل الإثبات، وهكذا إذا كان النفي مشتبه الحال لكن لا يعرف أن الراوي اعتمد دليل المعرفة، ولما لم يكن النفي مثل الإثبات فلا تعارض بينهما، بل الإثبات يكون مرجّحا ؛ لأنه أولى لكونه ثابتًا بالدليل. (السنبلي) إلى دفعه أي بالترجيح من وجه آخر (القمر) مذهب ابن أبان أي ثبوت التعارض بين المثبت والنافي والرجوع إلى الترجيح، وقال ابن الملك: إن ابن أبان كان من أصحاب الحديث ثم غلب عليه الرأي، تفقه على محمد بن الحسن، وكان موته سنة إحدى وعشرين ومائتين. (القمر) فلا يكون إلخ لأنه لا دليل على النفي، بل هو مبني على الاستصحاب الذي ليس بحجة. (القمر) مذهب الكرخي: أي ترجيح المثبت على النافي، قال ابن الملك: إن الكرخي ولد سنة ستين ومائتين، ومات سنة أربعين وثلاث مائة (القمر) مثالين أحدهما ما إذا كان النفي من جنس ما يعرف بدليله وثانيهما ما إذا كان يشتبه حاله لكن عرف أن الراوي اعتمد على دليل المعرفة. (القمر) فالنفي في حديث بريرة فيها، وهي التي كانت مكاتبة لعائشة لها، وكانت في نكاح عبد، فلما أدت بدل الكتابة قال لها رسول الله: ملكتِ بضعكِ فاختاري، ولكن اختلف في أنه حين خيرها هل بقي زوجها عبدًا أم صار حرًّا؟ فقيل: إنه كان عبدا على حاله، وهو مختار الشافعي حيث لا يثبت الخيار للمعتقة إلا إذا كان زوجها عبدًا، وقيل: قد صار حرا وهو مختار أبي حنيفة حيث يثبت الخيار للمعتقة سواء كان زوجها عبدًا أو حرًّا، فالحرية وإن كانت أصلية في دار الإسلام والعبودية عارضة، ولكن لما اتفقت الرواة ومثال بالجر معطوف على قوله مثالين (القمر) فالنفي في حديث إلخ تفريع على ما مهده من الأصل من قبول النفي في مسألتين وعدمه في مسألتين فذكر مسائل منها: لو أعتقت الأمة وزوجها حرّ فإن لها خيار العتق عندنا ولا خيار لها عند الشافعي، والاختلاف مبني على الاختلاف في زوج بريرة. [فتح الغفار: ۳۱۷] قال لها إلخ وثبت به أن الأمة المنكوحة إذا صارت معتقة كان لها خيار فسخ النكاح (القمر) اختلف والاختلاف في أنه كان عبدًا قبل أن خيرها. فقيل إنه كان إلخ في "الصحيحين" عن عائشة أن خيرها وكان زوجها عبدا. (القمر) على حاله إلخ وهذا الخبر نافٍ للحرية، وخبر الحرية مثبت لها، وإخبار العبدية إنما هو باعتبار الأصل؛ لأن عبديته كانت معلومة متقرّرة من قبل، فالإخبار بما بالأصل لعدم العلم بالحرية الطارئة، والإخبار بالحرية لا يصح إلا بعد العلم بوجودها عن دليل، فقدّم إخبار الحرية على إخبار نفيه أعني العبدية، وحكم بثبوت الخيار وإن كان الزوج حرا، وأن الخيار ليس لدفع عار كونها تحت العبد كما عليه الشافعية، بل السبب حرية الزوجة بعد المملوكية دفعا لزيادة الملك على نفسها، فإن الطلاق بالنساء كما يشهد به ما روى الدار قطني مرفوعًا "طلاق الأمة تطليقان، وعدتها حيضتان"، فواتح الرحموت. (السنبلي) وقيل قد صار إلخ: وقد عزاه في "التيسير" إلى الكتب الستة، كذا في "الصبح الصادق". (القمر) فالحرية إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره: أن الحرية أصل والعبودية عارضة في دار الإسلام، فخبر الحرية ليس مثبتا؛ فإنه ما ثبت أمرًا زائدا عارضا بل خبر العبودية مثبت؛ فإنه أثبت أمرًا عارضا زائدا. (القمر) قال الزيلعي: أخرجه الدار قطني عن عائشة، ولابن سعد في "الطبقات": وقد عتق بضعك معك فاختاري وهو مرسل على الشعبي، وروت عائشة قالت خُيّرت بريرة على زوجها حين عتقت، متفق عليه، وفي رواية النسائي: فخيرها رسول الله من زوجها، وكان عبدًا فاختارت نفسها. [إشراق الأبصار: ٢٤]
Chapter on Conflict. Explanation of the occurrence of conflict between two analogies. The principle thereof is that the negative, if it is of the kind known by its evidence, i.e., based on a clear proof and sign, and not based on istishab (presumption of continuity) which is not a valid proof, or if its situation is ambiguous but it is known that the narrator relied on evidence of knowledge, meaning the negative in itself could possibly be derived from evidence or based on istishab, but when the narrator's situation is examined, it is known that he relied on evidence and did not base it on mere apparent state, then in these two forms it is like the positive; because the positive is only established by evidence, so if the negative is also by evidence, it is like it, so they conflict, and thereafter it requires resolution. Then the madhhab of Ibn Aban comes. Otherwise, no – i.e., if the negative is not of the kind known by its evidence nor it is known that the narrator relied on evidence, but rather he based it on the previous apparent state, then it is not like the positive in opposing it, rather the positive is preferable because it is established by evidence. Then the madhhab of al-Karkhi comes. So we then need three examples: two examples in it (i.e., in conflict between positive and negative). (al-Qamar) on istishab i.e., continuing what was before. (al-Qamar) its situation is ambiguous etc. The meaning of ambiguous situation is that it is sometimes known by evidence and sometimes by the original state. (al-Sunbuli) these two forms etc., i.e., in the form of being of the kind known by its evidence and in the form of being ambiguous. His statement: like the positive etc. means the negative is like the positive, so both conflict – i.e., the negative and the positive – and preference for one of them is sought from outside to remove the conflict. And his statement: 'Otherwise, no' means if the negative is not one of the two mentioned categories, then the negative is not like the positive. Likewise if the negative is ambiguous but it is not known that the narrator relied on evidence of knowledge, and since the negative is not like the positive, there is no conflict between them, rather the positive is given preference because it is preferable for being established by evidence. (al-Sunbuli) to resolve it i.e., by preference from another aspect (al-Qamar) madhhab of Ibn Aban i.e., existence of conflict between positive and negative and resort to preference. Ibn al-Malik said: Ibn Aban was among the hadith scholars then he became predominantly of opinion; he studied fiqh under Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and died in the year 221 AH. (al-Qamar) so it is not etc. because there is no evidence for the negative, rather it is based on istishab which is not a proof. (al-Qamar) madhhab of al-Karkhi: i.e., preferring the positive over the negative. Ibn al-Malik said: al-Karkhi was born in 260 AH and died in 340 AH. (al-Qamar) two examples: one where the negative is of the kind known by its evidence, and the second where its situation is ambiguous but it is known that the narrator relied on evidence of knowledge. (al-Qamar) so the negative in the hadith of Barirah: she was a mukatibah of Aisha, and she was married to a slave. When she paid the kitabah, the Messenger of Allah said to her: 'You have ownership of yourself, so choose.' But there is disagreement: when he gave her the choice, did her husband remain a slave or become free? It was said: he remained a slave, which is the choice of al-Shafi'i, as he does not establish the option for the freed woman unless her husband is a slave. And it was said: he became free, which is the choice of Abu Hanifa, as he establishes the option for the freed woman whether her husband is a slave or free. So freedom, even if it is original in the lands of Islam and slavery is incidental, but when the narrators agreed ... and the example is in the genitive case, conjuncted to his statement 'two examples' (al-Qamar). So the negative in the hadith etc. is a branch of what he established from the principle of accepting the negative in two matters and not in two matters. So he mentioned matters including: if a slave woman is freed and her husband is free, then she has the option of emancipation according to us, and she has no option according to al-Shafi'i, and the difference is based on the difference concerning the husband of Barirah. [Fath al-Ghaffar: 317] He said to her etc. and it is established by it that the married slave woman, when she becomes freed, has the option to annul the marriage. (al-Qamar) there is disagreement, and the disagreement is whether he was a slave before he gave her the choice. So it was said he was etc. In the two Sahihs from Aisha that he gave her the choice and her husband was a slave. (al-Qamar) on his state etc. This report negates freedom, and the report of freedom affirms it. The report of slavery is based on the original state because his slavery was known and established previously, so the report according to the original is due to lack of knowledge of the supervening freedom, and the report of freedom is not valid except after knowledge of its existence from evidence. So the report of freedom is given precedence over the report of its negation, i.e., slavery, and the ruling is that the option is established even if the husband is free, and that the option is not for removing the disgrace of being under a slave as the Shafi'is hold, but rather the reason is the freedom of the wife after being owned, to prevent the increase of ownership over herself; for divorce belongs to women, as witnessed by what al-Daraqutni reported as marfu': 'The divorce of a slave woman is two divorces, and her iddah is two menstrual cycles.' (al-Sunbuli) And it was said he became etc. And in al-Taysir it is attributed to the six books. (al-Qamar) So freedom etc. A refutation of an anticipated objection: the objection is that freedom is original and slavery incidental in the lands of Islam, so the report of freedom is not affirmative; it does not establish an additional incidental matter, rather the report of slavery is affirmative because it establishes an additional incidental matter. (al-Qamar) Al-Zayla'i said: al-Daraqutni narrated it from Aisha, and Ibn Sa'd in al-Tabaqat: 'Your body has become free with you, so choose' and it is mursal from al-Sha'bi. And Aisha said: Barirah was given the choice regarding her husband when she was freed, agreed upon. In the narration of al-Nasa'i: The Prophet gave her choice from her husband, and he was a slave, so she chose herself. [Ishraq al-Absar: 24]
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage from Noorul Anwar discusses the rule of conflict (ta'arud) between positive (ithbat) and negative (nafi) evidence. The author first explains the principle: a negative statement can be considered equivalent to a positive statement in causing conflict if it meets one of two conditions: (1) it is based on a clear proof (dalil) and not merely on istishab (presumption of continuity), or (2) its basis is ambiguous but it is known that the narrator relied on evidence. In these two cases, the negative can conflict with the positive, and we must seek preference (tarjih) to resolve the conflict. This is the view of Ibn Aban. If the negative does not meet these conditions, it is not equivalent to the positive; the positive is given precedence because it is based on evidence. This is the view of al-Karkhi. The text then mentions the need for examples and provides the famous case of Barirah (ra). The hadith states that when Barirah was freed, the Prophet (saw) gave her the option (khiyar) to annul her marriage. The dispute is whether her husband was a slave or became free at that moment. Al-Shafi'i holds that the husband remained a slave, so the option is valid only if the husband is a slave; Abu Hanifa holds that the husband became free, so the option is valid regardless. The text explains that the report that the husband was a slave is a negative report (negating freedom) based on the original state (istishab), while the report that he became free is a positive report based on evidence. According to the rule, the positive report takes precedence over the negative, so Abu Hanifa's view is preferred. The commentary then clarifies that the option for the freed woman is not due to the shame of being married to a slave, but rather because of the increase in her status as a free person, giving her control over herself. This is supported by a hadith about the divorce of a slave woman.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict between two pieces of evidence that appear to lead to contradictory rulings, requiring resolution through tarjih or jam'.
نفي (nafi): A statement negating a specific ruling or attribute, e.g., 'Zayd is not free' or 'the husband was a slave'. In usul, it may be based on evidence or on istishab.
إثبات (ithbat): A statement affirming a specific ruling or attribute, e.g., 'Zayd is free' or 'the husband became free'. It is always based on evidence.
استصحاب (istishab): The presumption of continuity of a known state until evidence of change arises. It is deemed not to be a sufficient proof for establishing a new ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, a negative statement (nafi) creates a conflict with a positive (ithbat) requiring tarjih when:
A) It is reported in a sahih hadith.
B) It is based on istishab.
C) It is based on clear evidence or the narrator relied on evidence.
D) It comes from a narrator who is a mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a positive report is always given precedence over a negative report that is based solely on istishab, unless the negative is also supported by evidence.

Bayan al-Taghyir: Changing the Apparent Meaning
Defines bayan al-taghyir and gives its means

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define bayan al-taghyir, list its four means (condition, exception, attribute, goal), and apply it to identify how a general text is qualified without abrogation.

Core Idea
Bayan al-taghyir changes the apparent meaning without abrogating the text.

In Hanafi usul, bayan (clarification) has three types. The first two, bayan al-taqrir and bayan al-tafsir, confirm or explain the apparent meaning. The third, bayan al-taghyir, alters it through linguistic devices. This lesson unpacks the definition, examples, and how it differs from naskh.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the concept
Identify bayan al-taghyir as the third type of bayan that changes the apparent meaning (zahir) of a text.
It is not abrogation (naskh) because the original ruling remains applicable outside the qualified scope.
2
Memorize the four means
The text mentions four devices: condition (shart), exception (istithna'), attribute (sifah), and goal (ghayah). Each restricts or modifies the general application.
Example: 'Fulfill contracts' is general, but 'except contracts involving usury' is an exception.
3
Understand how each device changes meaning
A condition makes the ruling conditional; an exception excludes certain cases; an attribute narrows the subject; a goal limits the time or scope.
E.g., 'Kill polytheists' becomes 'Kill polytheists except those who seek asylum' via exception.
4
Distinguish from naskh
Naskh abrogates the original ruling entirely; taghyir leaves the original intact but qualified. Both change the result, but the mechanism differs.
The text also discusses ta'khir al-bayan (delayed clarification) but that is a separate topic.
5
Note intra-madhhab variations
Some Shafi'i scholars classify taghyir under bayan al-tafsir, but the Hanafi position maintains it as a distinct category.
The practical difference affects how one interprets general texts before qualification is revealed.

(القمر) فإذا قرأناه أي عليك يا محمد بقراءة جبرائيل فاتّبع ،قرآنه استمع قراءته (القمر) بيانه أي إظهار معاني القرآن ،وأحكامه وهذا هو بيان التفسير، والشارح الله حمل البيان على مطلق البيان حيث يدلّ على أن إلخ. Bayan al-taghyir: or bayan al-taghyir, like attachment to a condition and exception, for the condition delayed in mention like His saying: and the attribute and the goal. According to some mutakallimin from the Hanbalis and some Shafi'is like Abu Ishaq al-Marwazi and Abu Bakr al-Sayrafi... Or bayan al-taghyir: that is, changing the wording from the apparent meaning to something else. He said: and it is...
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage defines the third type of bayan: bayan al-taghyir (clarification by alteration). Unlike the previous two types that confirm or explain the apparent meaning, this type changes the apparent meaning of a statement by attaching a condition (shart), exception (istithna'), attribute (sifah), or goal (ghayah). For example, a general command may be qualified by a condition that limits its applicability. The text also mentions that some Hanbali and Shafi'i scholars hold a different view on certain aspects of ta'khir al-bayan, which is discussed in the marginal annotations. The core concept is that bayan al-taghyir does not abrogate the text but restricts or modifies its apparent meaning through linguistic devices.

Key Terms
بيان تغيير (bayān al-taghyīr): Clarification that alters the apparent meaning of a statement by means of a condition, exception, attribute, or goal.
تعليق بالشرط (ta‘līq bil-sharṭ): Attaching a condition to a ruling, which changes its scope, e.g., from unconditional to conditional.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Adding a condition to a general command
B) Adding an exception like 'except what is necessary'
C) Explaining the ambiguous term by Sunnah
D) Qualifying a command with an attribute

Key Takeaway
Bayan al-taghyir qualifies a text's apparent meaning via linguistic devices without abrogating it.

Connection Required for Explanatory Change (Bayan al-Taghyeer)
Condition for validity of explanatory change (bayan al-taghyeer)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a bayan al-taghyeer in a text and apply the Hanafi rule that it must be connected to be valid.

Core Idea
A condition or exception that changes a ruling is only effective if connected to the original statement.

In Hanafi usul, when a speaker first makes a general or immediate statement and then adds a condition or exception that changes its meaning, that addition is called bayan al-taghyeer. The key rule is that such explanatory changes must be connected (mawsul) to the prior statement. This lesson examines the examples of delayed conditions and exceptions, the proof from the oath hadith, and the refutation of the Ibn Abbas narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the examples
Locate the two examples: a delayed condition ('You are divorced if you enter the house') and a delayed exception ('He owes me one thousand except one hundred'). Notice how each changes the apparent meaning.
2
Understand the change
In the first example, the condition changes the ruling from immediate divorce to suspended divorce. In the second, the exception reduces the obligation from one thousand to nine hundred.
3
Grammatical reason
The passage states that condition and exception are 'dependent speech' (kalam ghair mustaqill) and do not convey meaning without what precedes, so they must be connected.
This is a linguistic argument.
4
Analyze the hadith proof
The Prophet's hadith makes expiation the only release from an oath. If disconnected exception were valid, it would provide an alternative release (saying 'in sha Allah' later) and contradict the hadith.
This is a dalil al-khitab argument: when the Lawgiver specifies one method, others are excluded.
5
Evaluate the counter-evidence
The narration from Ibn Abbas seems to allow disconnected exception. The Hanafi response interprets the 'after a year' report as a momentary pause (due to breathing or coughing), preserving the connection requirement.
This shows how Hanafis handle apparently conflicting evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان تغيير ] أو بيان تغيير كالتعليق بالشرط والاستثناء، فإن الشرط المؤخّر في الذكر مثل قوله : "أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار" بيان مغيّر لما قبله من التنجيز إلى التعليق؛ إذ لو لم يكن قوله: "إن دخلت الدار" يقع الطلاق في الحال، وبإتيان الشرط بعده صار معلقًا، بخلاف الشرط المقدم، فإنه ليس كذلك في رأينا، وهكذا الاستثناء في مثل قوله: "له علي ألف إلّا مائة" أي بيانا مغيرا غير وجوب المائة عن ذمته، ولو لم يكن قوله: "إلّا" مائة" لكان الواجب عليه ألفًا بتمامه. وإنما يصح ذلك موصولًا فقط؛ لأن الشرط والاستثناء كلام غير مستقل لا يفيد معنى بدون ما قبله، فيجب أن يكون موصولاً به، ولأنه عليها قال: "من حلف على يمين ورأى غيرها خيرًا منها فليكفّر عن يمينه ثم ليأتِ بالذي هو خيرا جعل مخلص اليمين هو الكفارة، ولو صح الاستثناء متراخيا لجعله مخلصًا أيضًا بأن يقول الآن إن شاء الله تعالى، أي الاستثناء ويبطل اليمين، وروي عن ابن عباس أنه يصح مفصولاً أيضًا لما روي أنه عليه قال: "الأغزُون" قريشًا " ثم قال بعد سنة: "إن شاء الله تعالى" ولا يجب الكفارة
Explanatory change (bayan al-taghyeer) is like conditioning by a condition and exception. For example, a delayed condition such as his saying 'You are divorced if you enter the house' is an explanatory change from immediate (effect) to suspended, because if he had not said 'if you enter the house', divorce would occur immediately; but with the condition after it, it becomes suspended. Unlike the advanced condition, which is not so in our view. Similarly, exception in his saying 'He owes me one thousand except one hundred' is an explanatory change removing the obligation of one hundred from his liability; without 'except one hundred', the full thousand would be owed. This is valid only when connected, because the condition and exception are dependent speech, not conveying meaning without what precedes, so they must be connected to it. Also because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever swears an oath and sees something better, let him expiate his oath and then do what is better.' He made expiation the release from the oath. If disconnected exception were valid, he would also make exception a release by saying now 'if Allah wills' and nullify the oath. And it is narrated from Ibn Abbas that it is valid disconnectedly as well, based on the narration that the Prophet said 'I will fight Quraysh' then said after a year 'if Allah wills' and no expiation is required.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage explains the category of bayan al-taghyeer, which changes the apparent meaning of a statement. Two examples are given: 1) A delayed condition like 'You are divorced if you enter the house'—the condition changes the immediate divorce to a suspended one. However, if the condition came before (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced'), it is not considered a change in the Hanafi view because the condition actually becomes part of the initial statement. 2) An exception like 'I owe one thousand except one hundred' changes the obligation to nine hundred. Both types are only valid when connected (mawsul) to the prior statement because condition and exception are grammatically dependent. The passage then provides a proof from the hadith about expiation: the Prophet made expiation the release from an oath, not exception. If disconnected exception were allowed, a person could simply say 'if Allah wills' after a delay and nullify the oath without expiation, which would contradict the hadith. It also mentions the report from Ibn Abbas allowing disconnection, but the Hanafi position rejects it by interpreting the long gap as momentary (due to breathing or coughing), not a true year-long delay.

Key Terms
بيان تغيير (bayan al-taghyeer): An explanation that changes the apparent meaning of a statement, such as by adding a condition or exception.
التنجيز (al-tanjeez): Immediate effect of a statement without any condition or delay.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): Suspending the effect of a statement upon fulfillment of a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is bayan al-taghyeer (e.g., exception) only valid when connected in Hanafi usul?
A) Because the exception is dependent speech and cannot stand alone
B) Because the Prophet forbade disconnection in all cases
C) Because the Quran requires it to be immediate
D) Because Ahmad ibn Hanbal ruled it invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, any explanatory change (bayan al-taghyeer) that alters the apparent meaning of a statement, such as a condition or exception, is only valid if it is connected to the initial statement; otherwise, the original ruling stands.

The Hanafi–Shafi‘i Dispute on Disconnected Specification (Takhsis Munfasil)
Explaining the Hanafi vs Shafi‘i dispute on specification of general terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi‘i positions on disconnected specification, identify the usul basis of the disagreement (Bayan Taghyir vs Bayan Taqrir), and apply the Hanafi analysis to a Quranic example (the cow verse).

Core Idea
Specification of a general (takhsis) is either change (taghyir) or confirmation (taqrir) — the Hanafi view requires connection because the general is certain until proven otherwise.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar delves into one of the most fundamental disputes in usul al-fiqh: the nature of specification of general terms. At stake is whether a later, disconnected statement can restrict a general command. The Hanafi school, holding that the general is certain, treats specification as a change requiring immediate connection, while Imam al-Shafi‘i, viewing the general as probable, allows separation. Through this debate, we also learn the critical distinction between takhsis al-amm and taqyid al-mutlaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
State the issue: can specification (takhsis) of a general term (amm) be performed with a disconnected (munfasil) stipulation, or must it be connected (muttasil)?
This dispute is between the Hanafi school (requires connection) and Imam al-Shafi‘i (allows disconnection).
2
Understand the Hanafi theory (Bayan Taghyir)
According to Hanafis, the general is qat'i (certain) in encompassing all its individuals. Specification changes it to zanni (probable), so it is a 'change' (taghyir) that requires the specifying evidence to be connected to the original statement, like exception (istithna').
This connection is necessary because the change in epistemic status must be immediate.
3
Understand the Shafi‘i theory (Bayan Taqrir)
Imam al-Shafi‘i holds that general terms are inherently zanni (probable) — 'there is no general that has not been specified'. Hence specification does not change the nature; it merely 'confirms' (taqrir) the probability already present, so it is valid both connectedly and disconnectedly.
The Shafi‘i view relies on empirical observation that general statements are almost always qualified.
4
Analyze the counterexample (cow verse)
The objection that Allah commanded 'slaughter a cow' (Quran 2:67) generally, then later specified its attributes, seems to support disconnected specification. The Hanafi response: 'cow' (baqarah) is an indefinite noun in an affirmative context (nakira fi mawdi' al-ithbat), which indicates a single individual — it is absolute (mutlaq), not general (amm). The subsequent clarifications are restrictions (taqyid) of the absolute, not specification of a general. Restriction of the absolute is considered like abrogation (naskh) of the absolute, which is valid disconnectedly.
This distinction is crucial: not every limited expression is 'amm; the grammatical category determines the usul treatment.
5
Apply the distinction
Given a text, determine whether it is a general term (amm) or an absolute (mutlaq). If it is amm, then any later disconnected specification is invalid according to Hanafis. If it is mutlaq, later restrictions are valid as taqyid al-mutlaq (which functions like naskh and can be disconnected). This distinction has practical implications for legal derivation (istinbat).
The key test: does the term encompass multiple individuals (amm) or refer to a single individual with unspecified attributes (mutlaq)?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

السؤال الثاني
وعنده ليس بتغيير إلخ وهذا الخلاف بين إمامنا والإمام الشافعي لما لها مبني على أن العام قطعي الثبوت في جميع ما يتناوله العام، فيكون تخصيص بعض مسمياته بيان تغيير، وهو لا يصح إلا موصولاً. أما عند الشافعي يحله فالعام ظني في مدلولاته وليس مستغرقا الجميع مسمياته كما قال له: ما من عام إلا وقد خُص عنه البعض، فيكون التخصيص بيان تقرير، وهو يجوز موصولاً ومفصولاً. (السنبلي) للظنية إلخ إيماء إلى أنه ليس المراد بالتقرير بيان التقرير المصطلح، وهو توكيد الكلام بما يقطع احتمال المجاز أو الخصوص، بل المراد من التقرير تقرير موجب العام، وهو الظنية. (القمر) حين طلبوا أن يعلموا إلخ قد قتل لهم قتيل لا يُدرى قاتله، وسألوا موسى عليه أن يدعو الله أن يبينه لهم، فقال موسى ل: إنَّ اللهَ يَأْمُرُكُمْ أَنْ تَذْبَحُوا
بقرة (البقرة: ٦٧) فيضرب القتيل ببعض البقرة، فيصير حيًّا، ويخبر بقاتله بينها الله تعالى: بأنها لا مُسنّة ولا صغيرة بل بين بين، صفراء، شديدة الصفرة، غير مُذلّلة بالعمل، مُسلّمة من العيوب لا لون فيها غير لونها. (القمر) :وهو: أي النكرة في موضع الإثبات وضعت إلخ أي ليست البقرة بعامة، بل وضعت لفرد واحد معين. وما في "مسير الدائر" من أنها وضعت لفرد واحد معين فزلة عن القلم. (القمر)
مطلقة فلذا سألوا عن تعيين الأوصاف (القمر) :فكان أي فكان البيان نسخا لإطلاقه. (القمر)
Chapter on the divisions of Bayan. Bayan of Change. This transmission is not authentic according to us, and it is narrated that Abu Ja'far ibn Mansur al-Dawaniqi, who was among the Abbasid caliphs, said to Abu Hanifa: Why did you oppose my grandfather in the impermissibility of disconnected exception? He said: 'If that were valid, may Allah bless your pledge, then people would say now: If Allah wills, and your pledge would be invalidated.' So al-Dawaniqi was perplexed and remained silent. And there is disagreement concerning the specification of the general: according to us, it does not occur disconnectedly; according to al-Shafi'i, it is permissible. This disagreement is in specification that is initial. But if the general has been specified once connectedly, it is permissible to specify it a second time disconnectedly, by agreement. And this is based on the fact that specification of the general according to us is Bayan of Change, so necessarily it is restricted to the condition of connection, while according to him it is Bayan of Confirmation, so it is valid both connectedly and disconnectedly. This transmission etc.: i.e., the transmission from Ibn 'Abbas is not authentic according to us. And if it were authentic, perhaps his meaning is that if a man intends exception at the time of utterance, then reveals his intention after utterance, his statement regarding what he intended is accepted in the inner court (between him and Allah), and his school is that what is accepted in the inner court is also accepted in the outward, as transmitted from al-Ghazali. And al-Qari said: Know that Ibn 'Abbas used to say the validity of exception separate from the excepted from even if time has passed, and Mujahid also held this. In some narrations from him that he estimated the length of time as six [months?], and if he excepted after that it becomes void, and there is a narration estimating it as six months and as a month. (al-Qamar) Not authentic etc. I say: Even if we accept the authenticity of this transmission, it does not indicate that he attached what he said a year before with this exception, because he attached [it] with what he said in that same session; he repeated that speech after a year and followed it connectedly in that session with that exception. In early Islam, he used to say 'I will do such-and-such tomorrow' and promise people, not saying 'If Allah wills', then when Allah forbade that and commanded him to use exception in promises, he adhered to exception in all promises. This is supported by the story of a man who asked him about the people of the Cave; he said 'I will tell you tomorrow' relying on revelation, but revelation did not come for a while, so he grieved, then the prohibition of promising without exception was revealed. (al-Sanbali) Does not occur disconnectedly: i.e., it is not permissible disconnectedly; rather it occurs and specification is permissible connected with the general. (al-Qamar) That: i.e., specification of the general disconnectedly. (al-Qamar) Be initial: i.e., without the general having been specified before this connectedly. (al-Qamar) Bayan of Change: because the general was certain (qat'i) according to us, and after specification it becomes probable (zanni), so specification changed it from certainty to probability. Bayan of Confirmation: because the general before specification was probable (zanni) according to him, and after specification also probable, so the specification confirms the probability, not changing it from certainty to probability. And one may say: Specification, even if it confirms the probability of the general, changes it from encompassing all individuals, for which it was placed, to particularity, which it was not placed for, so in this respect it is Bayan of Change. Reflect. (al-Qamar) Chapter on the divisions of Bayan. Bayan of Change. This is the meaning of what he said, and it is built on the fact that the general is like the particular according to us in necessitating the ruling with certainty, i.e., before specification. And after specification, certainty does not remain, so it was change, i.e., specification was Bayan of Change from certainty to probability, so it is restricted to the condition of connection. According to him, it is not change but rather confirmation of the probability that it had before specification, so it is valid both connected and disconnected. And since it is established according to us that specification of the general does not occur disconnectedly, three objections arise against us: First: That Allah first commanded the Children of Israel with a general cow when they asked to know the killer of their brother. He said: 'Indeed, Allah commands you to slaughter a cow' (2:67). Then when they tried to know its quantity, quality, and color, Allah explained it in detail as revealed: He specified the general here, i.e., the cow, disconnectedly. He pointed to the answer by saying: The explanation of the cow of the Children of Israel is of the type of restriction of the absolute, not of the type of specification of the general, because His word 'cow' is an indefinite noun in the position of affirmation, and it is specially placed for a single individual but absolute in terms of attributes, so it was abrogation, hence it was valid disconnectedly because abrogation only occurs disconnectedly. Second: That His statement (the second question)... And according to him it is not change, etc. And this disagreement between our Imam and Imam al-Shafi'i is based on that the general is certain (qat'i) in all that it encompasses, so specifying some of its members is Bayan of Change, and it is only valid connectedly. According to al-Shafi'i, however, the general is probable (zanni) in its indications and is not all-encompassing of all its members, as he said: There is no general that has not been specified partially. So specification is Bayan of Confirmation, and it is valid both connectedly and disconnectedly. (al-Sanbali) 'For probability' etc. alludes that what is meant by confirmation is not the technical Bayan al-Taqrir, which is reinforcing speech to remove the possibility of metaphor or specification; rather the confirmation here is confirming the import of the general, i.e., probability. (al-Qamar) 'When they asked to know' etc.: They had a slain person whose killer was unknown, and they asked Moses to supplicate Allah to make it known to them, so Moses said: 'Indeed, Allah commands you to slaughter a cow' (2:67) and strike the slain with part of the cow, then he would become alive and inform of his killer. Then Allah clarified it: that it is neither old nor young, but between the two, yellow, intensely yellow, not subjugated by work, free from defects, no other color in it. (al-Qamar) 'That is': i.e., the indefinite noun in the position of affirmation is placed... i.e., the cow is not general, but placed for a single specific individual. And what is in 'Musir al-Da'ir' that it is placed for a specific individual is a slip of the pen. (al-Qamar) 'Absolute' hence they asked about specification of attributes. (al-Qamar) 'So it was' i.e., the explanation was abrogation of its absoluteness. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage from Noorul Anwar expounds upon the division of Bayan (explanation) into Bayan Taghyir and Bayan Taqrir, specifically addressing a key dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The central issue is whether the specification (takhsis) of a general term (amm) can be done with a disconnected (munfasil) stipulation — separated in time from the original statement — or must be connected (muttasil). According to the Hanafis, a general term in its original state is certain (qat'i) in proving the ruling for all its individuals. When some individuals are specified out, the ruling for the remaining individuals becomes probable (zanni) because specification introduces the possibility that the general was not intended for all. Thus, specification is a change (taghyir) from certainty to probability, and just as abrogation (naskh) changes a ruling, it requires connection to the original statement (like exception made in the same speech). Imam al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, holds that general terms are inherently probable (zanni) from the outset — they are not all-encompassing with certainty, as he is known to say 'No general is left unpecified'. Therefore, specification does not change the nature; it merely confirms (taqrir) the probability already present. Hence, it is valid both connectedly and disconnectedly. The passage also addresses a historical anecdote between Abu Hanifa and the caliph al-Mansur regarding disconnected exception, showing the practical implications. Additionally, the common objection that the Quranic story of the cow (Bani Isra'il) seems to involve a specified command after a general one is answered by explaining that the word 'cow' there is an indefinite noun in an affirmative context (nakira fi mawdi' al-ithbat), which is not general but refers to a single individual, and the subsequent clarification is a restriction of the absolute (taqyid al-mutlaq) or abrogation of the absolute, not specification of a general. This highlights the Hanafi method of analyzing texts based on their linguistic and usul categories.

Key Terms
بيان تغيير (Bayan Taghyir): A type of bayan that changes the ruling from certainty to probability, specifically through takhsis al-amm.
بيان تقرير (Bayan Taqrir): A type of bayan that confirms the already probable nature of the ruling, as applied to takhsis al-amm according to Shafi'i.
تخصيص العام (Takhsis al-‘Amm): The act of excluding some individuals from the scope of a general term.
مطلق (Mutlaq): An unqualified term that indicates a single individual without restriction of attributes (as in nakira in affirmative context).
نسخ (Naskh): Abrogation of a ruling by a later revelation; in this context, restriction of the absolute is called naskh because it replaces the absolute with a qualified ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (as explained in the passage), why is disconnected specification (takhsis munfasil) of a general term invalid?
A) Because the general term is considered zanni from the beginning, so specification does not change its nature.
B) Because the general term is qat'i in encompassing all its individuals, so specification changes it to zanni and must be connected to preserve the change.
C) Because the Quran and Sunnah only allow connected specification.
D) Because of the story of Abu Hanifa and al-Dawaniqi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi requirement that specification (takhsis) of a general term must be connected (muttasil) stems from the principle that the general is qat'i, making specification a change that demands immediacy, unlike the Shafi'i view of the general as inherently zanni.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Bayan Taghyir: Definition and Qur'anic Examples
Defining bayan taghyir with examples and refuting the perception of takhsis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a case of bayan taghyir in a text and explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes it from takhsis al-amm.

Core Idea
Bayan taghyir does not change the ruling; it clarifies that the general term never included the exception.

In this lesson, we explore a subtle but crucial concept in Hanafi usul: bayan taghyir (explanatory change). At first glance, certain verses appear to specify a general term with a later revelation. However, the Hanafi scholars argue that in reality, the general term was always intended to exclude certain items. Through two compelling Qur'anic examples—Prophet Nuh's family and the objects of worship—you will learn to distinguish true specification from mere clarification of original intent. This distinction impacts our understanding of how divine legislation unfolds and how we interpret apparent conflicts in the text.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the apparent conflict
Identify a general term (e.g., 'ahl' or 'ma') that seems to include certain individuals, followed by a later verse that excludes them. This looks like takhsis al-amm (specification of a general).
Nuh's 'ahl' seems to include all his children; later verse says his son is not from his family.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the general term never embraced the excluded individuals. The later verse is not a specification but a clarification (bayan al-taqrir) of the intended meaning from the start.
Linguistic or contextual evidence (qarina) shows the term was restricted from the beginning.
3
Analyze the linguistic evidence
Examine the word 'ahl': it can mean followers in religion, not just blood relatives. The word 'ma' is primarily for non-rational beings. Thus, the apparent generality is only superficial.
Prophet Nuh's disbelieving son was not an 'ahl' in the religious sense; Jesus and angels are rational beings, so 'ma' does not include them.
4
Address the objection of the exception
If the term never included the exception, why is an explicit exception needed? The Hanafi response: the exception removes a false assumption (like Nuh's paternal assumption) or emphasizes the intended meaning.
In Nuh's case, the exception clarifies that even though he is a son, he is not part of the family in the relevant sense.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if it were takhsis, the ruling changes at the time of the later text; if it is bayan al-taqrir, the ruling was always the same. This impacts the theory of naskh and gradual legislation.
The Hanafi position preserves the idea that divine communication is consistent and unambiguous from the beginning.

فصل في أقسام البيان
بيان تغيير
خطاباً لنوح عليه: ﴿فَاسْلُكْ فِيهَا مِنْ كُلِّ زَوْجَيْنِ اثْنَيْنِ وَأَهْلَكَ﴾ أي أدخل في السفينة من كل جنس من الحيوان زوجين اثنين ذكرًا وأنثى، وأدخل أهلك أيضًا فيها، فالأهل عام متناول لكل أولاده، ثم خص منه كنعان بن نوح بقوله: ﴿إِنَّهُ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِكَ﴾ (هود: ٤٦) فقد خص العام متراخيًا ههنا أيضًا؟ فأجاب بقوله: والأهل لم يتناول الابن؛ لأن أهل النبي من كان تابعه في الدين والتفاوة لا من كان ذا نسب منه فلم يكن الابن الكافر أهلا له، لا أنه خص بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّهُ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِكَ﴾ حتى يكون تخصيص العام متراخيا، ولكن يرد عليه أنه تعالى استثنى ابنه أولًا بقوله: ﴿وَأَهْلَكَ إِلَّا مَنْ سَبَقَ عَلَيْهِ الْقَوْلُ﴾ (هود: ٤٠) فلو لم يكن الأهل متناولًا للابن لم يحتج إلى الاستثناء، هذا الجواب. (القمر)
فالأهل عام إلخ لأنه مضاف، ومثله مثل المعرف باللام. (القمر)
ويستشكل حينئذ بقول نوح عليه: ﴿وَرَبِّ إِنَّ ابْنِي مِنْ أَهْلِي﴾ (هود: ٤٥) ويجاب بأن نوحا كان يظن أنه موقن؛ لأنه كان من المنافقين؛ فلذا فهم أنه من الأهل، فتأمل. (القمر)
ولكن يرد إلخ: أقول في جواب الإيراد: إن المراد بالأهل ليس إلا من تابعه في الدين، والمراد بالمستثنى في قوله: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ سَبَقَ﴾ (هود: ٤٠) إلخ من لم يتبعه في الدين سواء كان ابنه أو غيره، لكن أصل كلمة "من" العموم، فصار كنعان ابنه داخلا في المستثنى من حيث عدم الإتباع والاستثناء ههنا استثناء منقطع، أو أقول: إن المراد بالأهل هو المتبع، والمراد بقوله: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ سَبَقَ﴾ (هود: ٤٠) إلخ هو ابنه؛ لأن كلمة "من" يحتمل التخصيص، والاستثناء متصل على التغليب كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَسَجَدَ الْمَلائِكَةُ كُلُّهُمْ أَجْمَعُونَ إِلَّا إِبْلِيسَ﴾ (الحجر: ٣١،٣٠) كان إبليس من الجن، :قلت ولما ثبت أن هذا ليس من قبيل تخصيص العام فمن أي قبيل هو ؟ أقول: ليس هو من قبيل بيان المجمل أيضًا؛ فإنه لا يجوز التأخير فيه عن وقت الحاجة، وههنا قد تأخر عن وقت الحاجة، وههنا قد تأخر عن وقت الامتثال بالأمر بالإركاب، بل هو من قبيل بيان التقرير فإن المراد بالأهل الأتباع بالقرينة وأمره عليه ابنه بالركوب إما لزعم الإيمان لكونه كافرًا منافقاً، أو حمل الأهل على ذي النسب بالاجتهاد، فقرر الله تعالى ما أراده؛ ولذا عاتبه على الخطأ وهو تعوّذ أو المراد الأهل القريب سببًا ونسبًا لقرينة ما كانت والابن داخل في المستثنى، وهو عالما بأن المراد من "مَن "سبق" الكفار لكن كان يظن الله إياه مؤمنًا لنفاقه داخلا في الباقي بعد الاستثناء، "ومن سبق عليه القول" مختصا بامرأته، ولا ذنب في هذا الخطأ بالاجتهاد، ۱۲ كذا في "المعتبرات". (السنبلي)
عليه أي على قوله والأهل لم يتناول الابن. (المحشي)
عليه القول: أي قول الحق منهم بالإهلاك هو زوجته وولده كنعان. (القمر)
وكان في النسب مرادًا لما احتيج إلى الاستثناء، ولكن نوحا عليه لم يتفطن له لغاية شفقته عليه حتى سأل من الله تعالى: ﴿وَرَبِّ إِنَّ ابْنِي مِنْ أَهْلِي وَإِنَّ وَعْدَكَ الْحَقُّ وَأَنْتَ أَحْكَمُ الْحَاكِمِينَ قَالَ يَا نُوحُ إِنَّهُ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِكَ إِنَّهُ عَمَلٌ غَيْرُ صَالِحٍ﴾ (هود: ٤٦،٤٥)
الثالث: أن قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّكُمْ وَمَا تَعْبُدُونَ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ حَصَبُ جَهَنَّمَ﴾ (الأنبياء: ٩٨) كلمة "ما" عامة لكل معبود سواه، فقال عبد الله بن الزبعري: أليس أن عيسى عليه وعزير والملائكة قد عُبدوا من دون الله، أَفَتَراهُمْ يُعذبون في النار؟ فنزل قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ سَبَقَتْ لَهُمْ مِنَّا الْحُسْنَى أُولَئِكَ عَنْهَا مُبْعَدُونَ﴾ (الأنبياء: ١٠١)، فخص كلمة "ما" بهذه الآية متراخيا؟ فأجاب بقوله: وقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّكُمْ وَمَا تَعْبُدُونَ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ﴾ لم يتناول عيسى عليه، لا أنه خص بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ سَبَقَتْ لَهُمْ مِنَّا الْحُسْنَى﴾؛ لأن أي من الأصل كلمة "ما" لذوات غير العقلاء، وعيسى عليه ونحوه لم يدخل في عموم كلمة "ما".
ولكن نوحًا إلخ : دفع لتوهّم الناشئ من الكلام السابق، وهو: أنه لما استثنى من سبق عليه القول من الأهل، والمراد به كنعان فلم سأل نوح عليه نجاته؟ وحاصل الدفع أن نوحا لغاية شفقته على كنعان لم يتفطن له، ولم يلتفت إلى أن المراد بالمستثنى كنعان وإن كان يعلم كفره. وفيه أن هذا عجيب من الأنبياء عليهم السلام، فالأوجه أن يقال: إن نوحًا عليه علم أن المراد بمَنْ سبق عليه القول الكفار وابنه كان منافقا يبطن الكفر ويظهر الإيمان بمشافهة نوح عليه أنه مؤمن، فظن نوح من أهله، فدعاه نوح عليه إلى السفينة، فلما غرق تحير نوح عليه وسأل ربه وقال رب إلخ. كذا قال بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي الله (القمر)
وإن وعدك: وهو نجاة أهل نوح. (القمر)
عمل إلخ : أي إن سؤالك يا نوح، بنجاة الابن عمل غير صالح. (القمر)
حصب إلخ : الحصب الوقود أي ما يرمي به إليها وتهيج به. (القمر)
فقال عبد الله بن إلخ : أي من رسول الله كذا قال العسقلاني. وكان كافرًا يهوديًا ذلك الزمان، والزِّبَعْرَي بكسر الزاء المعجمة وفتح الموحدة وسكون العين المهملة، وعن عبيدة فتح الراء. كذا في الصبح الصادق (القمر)
أليس أن عيسى إلخ فإنه عبده النصارى، وعزير عبده اليهود، والملائكة عبدهم بنو المليح. (السنبلي)
لا أنه خص إلخ : فإن التخصيص فرع الدخول، وإذا ليس فليس. (القمر)
لذوات غير العقلاء إلخ فيه أن ما تعمّ لذوي العقول وغيرهم على رأى الأكثرين على ما مر، فهذا الجواب ليس بصحيح على رأيهم، وقيل في الجواب: أن يقال: إن الخطاب في آية ﴿إِنَّكُمْ وَمَا تَعْبُدُونَ﴾ (الأنبياء:٩٨) إلى قريش مكة، وكانوا عابدي الأصنام، فمعنى الآية إنكم يا كفار قريش ﴿وَمَا تَعْبُدُونَ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ﴾ (الأنبياء: ۹۸) وهي الأصنام حصب جهنم، فعيسى وعزير والملائكة ليسوا بداخلين في هذه الآية، وقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ سبقت (الأنبياء: ١٠١) إلخ كلام مبتدأ لبيان أن شأنهم رفيع، وقياسهم على معبوداتكم لا يجوز. (القمر)
Section on the divisions of Bayan: Bayan Taghyir. Addressing Nuh (peace be upon him): 'Then embark therein of each kind two, two, and your family' meaning bring into the ark from every species of animal two pairs, male and female, and also bring your family. So 'family' is general encompassing all his children. Then it was specified from it Kan'an son of Nuh by His saying: 'Indeed, he is not of your family' (Hud:46). So the general was specified later here as well? He answered: 'And 'family' did not include the son, because the family of a prophet is whoever followed him in religion and piety, not whoever was of his lineage, so the disbelieving son was not his family. It is not that it was specified by His saying 'Indeed, he is not of your family' so that there is specification of the general later.' But it is objected that He first excluded his son by His saying: 'And your family, except those against whom the word has preceded' (Hud:40). If 'family' did not include the son, there would be no need for the exception...
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage defines 'Bayan Taghyir' (explanatory change) within the Hanafi usul framework. The author opens by stating the section heading. He then presents two Qur'anic examples that superficially appear to be instances of takhsis al-amm (specification of a general term by a later text) but which he argues are actually cases of bayan al-taqrir (clarification of the originally intended meaning). The first example involves Prophet Nuh's family: the verse commands him to take his 'ahl' (family) into the ark. Later, Allah says that his son is not from his family. The author argues that 'ahl' here never included the disbelieving son because the term refers to followers in religion, not mere blood relations. Hence, the later verse is not a specification but an explanation of the intended meaning. The second example is the verse 'Indeed, you and what you worship besides Allah are fuel of Hell.' The polytheist Ibn al-Ziba'ra objected that Jesus, Ezra, and angels were worshipped, so they would be in Hell. The response is that the word 'ma' is for non-rational beings, so these worshiped beings were never included in the general term. The later verse 'Indeed, those for whom the best [reward] has preceded from Us are far from it' is thus not a specification but a clarification. The commentary then discusses alternative interpretations and defenses of these positions, including the possibility that the exception in Nuh's case was a disconnected exception (munqati') or that Nuh was mistaken due to his son's hypocrisy. The author concludes that this type of bayan is better termed 'bayan al-taqrir' because it clarifies what was already intended, not changes the scope.

Key Terms
بيان تغيير (bayan taghyir): A type of bayan that appears to change the ruling of a general text but actually clarifies the originally intended meaning; it is not a change but an explanation.
تخصيص العام (takhsis al-amm): The specification of a general term by a later text that removes some of its apparent scope.
بيان التقرير (bayan al-taqrir): A clarification that the intended meaning from the beginning was the restricted one, even if the apparent general term seemed otherwise.
قرينة (qarina): Contextual evidence that indicates the intended meaning of a term, often preventing false generality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that the verse 'Indeed, those for whom the best has preceded' (Anbiya':101) is not a specification of the general term in 'Indeed, you and what you worship' (Anbiya':98)?
A) Because 'what you worship' is specific to idols worshipped by Quraysh.
B) Because the word 'ma' is for non-rational beings, so rational beings like Jesus were never included.
C) Because the later verse is about believers, not about the objects of worship.
D) Because the verse was revealed before the objection was made.

Key Takeaway
Bayan taghyir is not a change in the law; it reveals that the original general term was always intended in a restricted sense, and the later text simply clarifies that intention.

Linguistic Scope of 'Ma' in Quranic Exception
Analyzing the scope of 'ma' to rebut delayed specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the word 'ma' is exclusively for non-rational beings to determine the scope of a general Quranic verse and differentiate it from the need for delayed specification (takhsis mutarakhi).

Core Idea
The word 'ma' is for non-rational beings; it never includes rational beings like Jesus or angels.

This passage addresses a powerful objection raised by Abdullah ibn al-Ziba'ra against the Quranic verse 'Indeed you and what you worship besides Allah are fuel of Hell.' He argued that if the verse is general, it would include Jesus, Uzair, and angels. The Hanafi response, rooted in linguistic precision, shows that the word 'ma' never included them in the first place. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct usul analysis and avoids the need for hypothetical delayed specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Apparent Problem
Ibn al-Ziba'ra thought the general word 'ma' included all objects of worship, so he raised the objection about Jesus and angels.
2
Understand the Hanafi Answer
The Hanafi position is that the verse never included rational beings because 'ma' is only for non-rational beings.
This is based on the original linguistic usage (wad').
3
Learn the Linguistic Rule
In Arabic, 'man' (مَنْ) is for rational beings, 'ma' (مَا) for non-rational. The Quran uses 'ma' in the verse, so it excludes rational beings.
This rule is agreed upon by most grammarians, but some allow 'ma' for rational in certain contexts; Hanafis insist on the original exclusivity.
4
Apply the Rule to the Objection
Since Jesus, Uzair, and angels are rational, they were never included in the scope of 'ma'. Thus, no delayed specification (takhsis mutarakhi) is needed.
The later verse about 'those for whom good has preceded' is not a specification but a separate ruling.
5
Recognize the Usul Implication
The principle: A general word is understood according to its linguistic reality unless evidence shifts it. Here, the linguistic reality excludes rationals, so the general rule is not overridden.
This strengthens the Hanafi methodology of preferring original meanings (haqiqah) over claimed generalities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أقسام البيان
بيان تغيير
في النسب مرادًا لما احتيج إلى الاستثناء، ولكن نوحا عليه لم يتفطن له لغاية شفقته عليه حتى سأل من الله تعالى: ﴿وَرَبِّ إِنَّ ابْنِي مِنْ أَهْلِي وَإِنَّ وَعْدَكَ الْحَقُّ وَأَنْتَ أَحْكَمُ الْحَاكِمِينَ قَالَ يَا نُوحُ إِنَّهُ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِكَ إِنَّهُ عَمَلٌ غَيْرُ صَالِحٍ﴾، الثالث: أن قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّكُمْ وَمَا تَعْبُدُونَ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ حَصَبُ جَهَنَّمَ﴾ كلمة "ما" عامة لكل معبود سواه، فقال عبد الله بن الزبعري: أليس أن عيسى وعزير والملائكة قد عُبدوا من دون الله، أَفَتَراهُمْ يُعذبون في النار؟ فنزل قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ سَبَقَتْ لَهُمْ مِنَّا الْحُسْنَى أُولَئِكَ عَنْهَا مُبْعَدُونَ﴾، فخص كلمة "ما" بهذه الآية متراخيا؟ فأجاب بقوله: وقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّكُمْ وَمَا تَعْبُدُونَ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ﴾ لم يتناول عيسى عليه، لا أنه خص بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ سَبَقَتْ لَهُمْ مِنَّا الْحُسْنَى﴾؛ لأن كلمة "ما" من الأصل لذوات غير العقلاء، وعيسى عليه ونحوه لم يدخل في عموم كلمة "ما"
Section on the divisions of bayan. Bayan of alteration: Intended in the lineage, exception was needed, but Noah, peace be upon him, did not realize it due to his extreme compassion for him until he asked Allah: 'My Lord, indeed my son is of my family...' He said, 'O Noah, indeed he is not of your family; indeed he is an unrighteous deed.' Third: That Allah's saying, 'Indeed you and what you worship besides Allah are fuel of Hell'—the word 'ma' is general for every object of worship besides Him. So Abdullah ibn al-Ziba'ra said: 'Are not Jesus and Uzair and the angels worshipped besides Allah? Do you think they will be punished in Hell?' Then Allah revealed: 'Indeed those for whom the good [reward] has preceded from Us will be far removed from it.' So did He specify the word 'ma' by this verse delayed? He answered: His saying, 'Indeed you and what you worship besides Allah' did not include Jesus, peace be upon him, not that it was specified by His saying, 'Indeed those for whom the good has preceded from Us', because the word 'ma' originally is for non-rational beings, and Jesus and the like did not enter into the general meaning of the word 'ma'.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis demonstrating that the word 'ma' (ما) in Arabic is for non-rational beings, and thus the verse 'Indeed you and what you worship besides Allah are fuel of Hell' never included rational beings like Jesus, Uzair, or angels. The objection of Ibn al-Ziba'ra, who thought it did, is answered by clarifying the linguistic scope: since 'ma' excludes rationals, there is no need for delayed specification (takhsis mutarrakhi) by the later verse. This is a key Hanafi usul point that the general word is understood according to its original linguistic meaning unless there is clear evidence to the contrary.

Key Terms
ما (ma): The Arabic word for 'what', used for non-rational beings.
مَنْ (man): The Arabic word for 'who', used for rational beings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the verse was abrogated by a later one.
B) Because the word 'ma' is exclusively for non-rational beings, and Jesus is rational.
C) Because Jesus was not worshipped as a deity.
D) Because the verse only applies to the polytheists of Mecca.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle: The original meaning of a word governs its scope; 'ma' is for non-rational beings, so the verse never included rational beings like Jesus.

Hanafi and Shafi'i Views on Exception (Istithna)
Defining and comparing the operation of exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i mechanisms of exception (istithna) and apply the difference to a case where the excepted item is of a different genus.

Core Idea
Hanafis treat exception as if the excepted was never spoken; Shafi'is treat it as a cancellation by opposition.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar delves into the operation of exception (istithna), a key tool for clarifying general statements. The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on how exception works: is it a mere non-speaking of the excepted, or does it involve a contradiction between affirmation and negation? Understanding this distinction has practical consequences, especially when the excepted item differs in genus from the excluded-from.

Guided Path
1
Recognize istithna as bayan al-taghyeer
Identify that exception (istithna) is a type of demonstrative change (bayan al-taghyeer) that modifies the ruling of a prior statement.
It is contrasted with condition (shart) which also modifies.
2
Understand the Hanafi concept: preventing speech
According to Hanafis, exception 'prevents speech' regarding the excepted amount; it is as if the speaker never mentioned the excepted part. The ruling applies only to the remainder.
Example: 'I owe you a thousand dirhams except a hundred' is equivalent to 'I owe you nine hundred.'
3
Grasp the Shafi'i concept: mu'arada (opposition)
The Shafi'i school holds that exception works by opposition: the excepted is initially affirmed, then the exception negates it, causing the affirmation and negation to conflict and fall away.
Proof: 'La ilaha illa Allah' – the negation and affirmation oppose each other.
4
Apply the difference to a mixed-genus case
Consider 'I owe you a thousand dirhams except a garment.' Hanafis deem the exception invalid because the garment is of a different genus; thus he owes the full thousand. Shafi'is accept the exception and deduct the value of the garment.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
5
Critique the Shafi'i view from Hanafi perspective
The text notes a 'defect' (khidsha) in the Shafi'i view: the consensus of linguists that exception from affirmation is negation supports the Hanafi view. Moreover, the Shafi'i approach leads to convoluted reasoning when the excepted differs in genus.
The Hanafi view avoids this complication.

Source Text

(القمر) للتوحيد : أي الإقرار بوجوده تعالى ووحدته. (القمر)
Chapter on Types of Bayan. Mention of types of Bayan al-Taghyeer. But Ibn al-Ziba'ri only asked out of obstinacy and stubbornness, so the Prophet ﷺ said to him: How ignorant you are of the language of your people! Do you not know that 'ma' is for non-rational beings and 'man' for rational beings? Mention of types of Bayan al-Taghyeer. Since Bayan al-Taghyeer is divided into condition and exception, and the explanation of condition has passed in the discussion along with its ruling, the exception (mustathna) the corrupt aspects left its mention, and he engaged in the discussion of exception, saying: Exception prevents speaking about its ruling to the extent of the excepted [item], related to speech, as if he said: Exception prevents speaking to the extent of the excepted, as if he did not speak about the excepted at all, so it makes speech about the remainder after it, i.e., after the exception. So if he says, 'I owe him a thousand dirhams except a hundred,' it is as if he said, 'I owe him nine hundred,' and the amount of the hundred is as if he did not speak about it meaning, and did not rule upon it, just as in conditional suspension one does not speak about the consequence until the condition occurs. But Ibn al-Ziba'ri etc. is a response to what might be imagined that Ibn al-Ziba'ri is a linguist, so why did he not understand that the word 'ma' is for non-rational beings, and why did he ask what he asked? (al-Qamar) The Prophet said etc.: The author of al-Muslim said: It is not known that he said to him: 'How ignorant you are of the language of your people, ma is for what does not reason' so it has no basis as we explained before; so no one can say that he عليه said in repelling Ibn al-Ziba'ri's objection 'How ignorant you are' etc.; so the verse was not revealed to repel his objection such that it would be made specific, but rather it is a response to those who permit deferment in specification: we do not accept its generality absolutely for all worshipped beings, but rather its generality is only for the worshipped of the addressees, and they are the people of Mecca and they are the idols, so it did not include Jesus عليه and the angels and Ezra عليه, so his objection is stubbornness, and the revelation of His statement: 'Indeed those for whom the best [reward] has preceded' (al-Anbiya 101) etc. is a declaration of what is known of their non-inclusion, or to establish a statement of their distance from them, let alone inclusion in it, to cut off the stubbornness of the wretched. (al-Sanbali) As if he did not speak about it etc.: so the excluded-from remains in its lexical meaning, and it has been restricted by excluding the excepted, so a restrictive concept is obtained, which is an expression for the remainder after exception. So 'a thousand dirhams except a hundred' is an expression for nine hundred, but it is an expression for something with a longer wording, and there is no harm in that; for the speaker chooses to express what is in his mind with a longer or shorter phrase. (al-Qamar) He did not speak about the consequence etc. as when you say: 'You are divorced if you enter the house' so it is as if he did not speak about his statement 'You are divorced' until the condition occurs, so if the condition occurs, it is as if he spoke about his statement 'You are divorced' and its ruling applies. (al-Qamar) Bahr al-Ulum (may Allah illumine his grave) said in Tanwir al-Minar: The hadith scholars have discussion about this hadith until they said it is fabricated, and Ali narrated from al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani: It has no basis, neither from authentic nor weak chains. [Ishraq al-Absar: 25] al-Qari. And according to al-Shafi'i, it prevents the ruling by way of opposition, meaning that the excepted was first ruled upon in the previous speech, then it is taken out by way of opposition, so the appreciation of his statement: 'So-and-so owes me a thousand dirhams except a hundred' is that they are not owed to me; for the opening of the speech makes them obligatory and the exception negates them, so they oppose each other, i.e., the hundred, and they fall away. And it is said: Its benefit appears when one makes an exception of a different genus, like his statement: 'So-and-so owes me a thousand dirhams except a garment' so according to us the exception is not valid because it is not valid as a bayan, while according to him it is valid, so he deducts from the thousand the value of the garment; because the operation of exception is like a contradictory evidence, and it is according to possibility, and the possibility here is in negating the amount of its value. And this is not free from a defect due to the consensus of the linguists that exception from negation is affirmation and from affirmation is negation. This is a proof for al-Shafi'i that the operation of exception is by way of opposition, because negation and affirmation oppose each other together. And because his statement 'La ilaha illa Allah' is for tawhid, and its meaning. By way of opposition etc.: so the excepted indicates a ruling opposing the previous ruling. (al-Qamar) They oppose each other and fall away etc. so it prevents the previous ruling, which is the imposition on the hundred, rather the imposition which is the previous ruling is on the remainder, which is nine hundred. (al-Sanbali) They fall away: so the ruling is not established on the excepted. (al-Qamar) Because it is not valid as a bayan: due to it being of a different genus. (al-Qamar) In negating etc.: i.e., in negating the amount of the value of the garment from the thousand. (al-Qamar) A defect perhaps that if the garment must be returned to the value to validate the exception, then there is no need to make the exception an opposition, but rather to make it an expression of what is beyond the excepted, as it was said. And it was said: The defect is that the operation of exception by opposition according to al-Shafi'i is only in the connected, and this is of the type of disconnected. (al-Qamar) A defect etc.: i.e., making the validity of exception in this case a fruit of al-Shafi'i's saying is not free from weakness; because opposition is only realized in one place, and here they are different; because the ruling in the opening of the speech is about dirhams and its negation after it is about the garment. Or we say: The face of the defect is that even if we accept that the operation of exception is like contradictory evidence, we do not accept that observance of exception is obligatory upon you in every case, and considering opposition in it obligates you according to possibility wherever the particle of exception is found. But if affirmation and negation are realized in one place in the case of exception, then its ruling according to you is falling away, and there is no need to consider opposition according to possibility such that we assume opposition here by consideration of the value of the garment. (al-Sanbali) By way of opposition: i.e., that the ruling of exception opposes the previous ruling. (al-Qamar) For tawhid: i.e., acknowledgment of His existence and oneness. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the types of bayan, specifically bayan al-taghyeer (demonstrative change) through exception (istithna). The author explains the Hanafi position first: exception operates by 'preventing speech' regarding the excepted part, as if the speaker never mentioned it. Thus, saying 'I owe you a thousand dirhams except a hundred' is legally equivalent to saying 'I owe you nine hundred dirhams.' The excepted amount is treated as never spoken. This is contrasted with conditional statements where the consequence is not spoken until the condition occurs. The passage then addresses an objection raised by Ibn al-Ziba'ri regarding the Prophet's use of 'ma' for idols, clarifying that the Prophet's response was not part of revelation but a reproach for ignorance. Later, the Shafi'i view is presented: exception works by mu'arada (opposition), meaning the excepted part was initially affirmed, then the exception negates it, so the two conflict and fall away. The practical difference appears when the excepted item is of a different genus (e.g., dirhams except a garment). Hanafis reject such exception as invalid because it cannot serve as bayan (clarification) when the genus differs. Shafi'is accept it, deducting the value of the garment from the total. The passage critiques the Shafi'i view by noting that the linguistic consensus that exception from affirmation is negation supports the Hanafi position, and the Shafi'i approach leads to convoluted reasoning when the excepted item differs in genus.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithna'): A type of bayan al-taghyeer that excludes part of the statement, making it as if the excepted was never spoken (Hanafi) or opposing the previous ruling (Shafi'i).
المعارضة (al-mu'arada): The Shafi'i concept that exception opposes the initial affirmation, causing the two to conflict and fall away.
بيان التغيير (bayan al-taghyeer): Demonstrative change: a type of bayan that modifies the ruling of a prior statement, including condition (shart) and exception (istithna).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the effect of saying 'I owe you a thousand dirhams except a hundred'?
A) The hundred dirhams are negated by opposition, causing the affirmation and negation to fall away.
B) The hundred dirhams are considered as never spoken, so the speaker owes nine hundred dirhams.
C) The hundred dirhams are deducted, but the ruling on the thousand remains applicable.
D) The exception is invalid because it is of a different genus.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school views exception as a non-speaking of the excepted, while the Shafi'i school views it as an opposition that nullifies the initial affirmation.
